Shaghil vs Mashghul: The Hanafi Rule for Gifts
Differentiating between a gifted object occupying donor's property and being occupied by it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shaghil and mashghul gifts and apply the Hanafi rule to determine the validity of a gift.

Core Idea
A gift is valid if the gifted object occupies the donor's property, but invalid if it is occupied by the donor's property.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi gift law: whether the gifted object is occupying (shaghil) the donor's property or occupied by it (mashghul). The ruling hinges on possession (qabd) being a condition for completion of a gift. We will explore examples from the text and see how the principle applies to various cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Learn the terms shaghil (occupying) and mashghul (occupied). The gifted object can either occupy the donor's property or be occupied by it.
Shaghil: e.g., food in a bag (food is shaghil). Mashghul: e.g., a bag containing food (bag is mashghul).
2
Understand the principle
The occupation of the gifted object by the donor's property prevents the completion of the gift because possession cannot be fully achieved. Occupation of the donor's property by the gifted object does not prevent completion.
The text: 'inna ishtighal al-mawhub bi-milk al-wahib yamna' tamam al-hibah'.
3
Apply to examples from the text
Work through the examples: gifting a bag with food (invalid), gifting food in a bag (valid), gifting a saddled animal (invalid), gifting the saddle alone (valid).
In each case, determine which is shaghil and which is mashghul.
4
Extend to cases where the occupant is not the donor's property
If the gifted object is occupied by something belonging to someone else (e.g., a house with a borrower's goods), the gift is valid because the obstacle is the donor's property, not another's.
The text provides examples of a lent house with goods placed by the borrower.
5
Note the same rule applies to mortgage and charity
The text concludes that the same principle applies to rahn (mortgage) and sadaqa (charity) because possession is a condition for their completion as in gifts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲] قوله : بالقبض الكامل ؛ ولو كان الموهوب شاغلاً لملك الواهب لا مشغولاً به، قال في «الفصول العمادية» في «فتاوى ظهير الدين» له : هبة الشاغل تجوز، وهبة المشغول لا تجوز. والأصل في جنس هذه المسائل : إنَّ اشتغال الموهوب بملك الواهب يمنع تمام الهبة ؛ لأنَّ القبض شرط ، وأمَّا اشتغالُ ملك الواهب بالموهوب فلا يمنع تمامَ الهبة ، مثاله : وهب جراباً فيه طعام لا يجوز، ولو وهب طعاماً في جراب جاز، وعلى هذا نظائره. وفي «الزيادات» المنسوب إلى القاضي أبي جعفر ه : لـو وهـب دابة مُسَرَّجَةً وسَلَّمَها كذلك لم يجز الهبة، وبمثله لو وهب اللجامَ والسرج دون الدابة وسلّمها كذلك جاز ؛ لأنَّ الدابة تصير مشغولة بالسرج واللجام ، والسرج واللجامُ لا يصير مشغولاً بالدابة، وعلى هذا الرهن. واشتغال الموهوب بملك غير الواهب، هل يمنع تمام الهبة؟ ذكر صاحب «المحيط» : في «الباب الأول من هبة» «الزيادات»: إنّه لا يمنع ، فإنه قال : لو أعار داراً من إنسان ثمَّ إنَّ المستعير غصب متاعاً ووضعه في الدار، ثم وهب المعير الدار من المستعير صحتِ الهبة في الدار. وكذلك لو أنَّ المعير هو الذي غصب المتاع ووضعه في الدار ، ثم وهب المعير من المستعير كانت الهبة تامة، وإن تبين أن الدار مشغولة بما ليس بموهوب لما لم تكن مشغولة بملك الواهب، وهو المانع من تمام الهبة. وكذلك لو وهب داراً بما فيها من المتاع، أو وهـب جـوالـق بما فيه من المتاع ، وسلّمها إلى الموهوب ثم استحق المتاع، فالهبة تامة في الجوالق والدار ؛ لأنَّ يد الواهب كانت ثابتة على الدار، والمتاعُ جميعاً حقيقة فصح تسليمه إياها إلى الموهوب. ثم باستحقاق المتاعِ إن تبين أنَّ المتاعَ لم يكن ملك الواهب لم يتبين أن الدار كانت مشغولة بملك الواهب، وهو المانع من تمام القبض، وكل جواب عرفته في هبة الدار والجوالق بما فيها فهو الجواب في الرهن والصدقة ؛ لأنَّ القبض شرط تمامها كالهية. انتهى.
[2] His saying: 'by complete possession' — even if the gifted object is occupying the donor's property, not occupied by it. He said in 'al-Fusul al-Imadiyya' from 'Fatawa Zahir al-Din': The gift of an occupying object is permissible, while the gift of an occupied object is not permissible. The principle in these types of issues is: The occupation of the gifted object by the donor's property prevents the completion of the gift, because possession is a condition. As for the occupation of the donor's property by the gifted object, it does not prevent the completion of the gift. Example: If he gifts a bag containing food, it is not valid; if he gifts food in a bag, it is valid. And on this are its analogs. And in 'al-Ziyadat' attributed to Judge Abu Ja'far: If he gifts a saddled animal and hands it over likewise, the gift is not valid. Similarly, if he gifts the bridle and saddle without the animal and hands them over likewise, it is valid, because the animal becomes occupied by the saddle and bridle, while the saddle and bridle do not become occupied by the animal. And on this is the mortgage. And the occupation of the gifted object by what is not the property of the donor — does it prevent the completion of the gift? The author of 'al-Muhit' mentioned in 'al-Bab al-Awwal min al-Hiba' of 'al-Ziyadat': It does not prevent. For he said: If someone lends a house to a person, then the borrower wrongfully takes goods and places them in the house, then the lender gifts the house to the borrower, the gift of the house is valid. Similarly, if the lender himself is the one who wrongfully took the goods and placed them in the house, then the lender gifts to the borrower, the gift is complete, even if it becomes clear that the house is occupied by what is not the gifted object, because it was not occupied by the donor's property, which is the preventer of the gift's completion. And similarly, if he gifts a house along with the goods in it, or gifts a sack along with the goods in it, and hands them over to the donee, then the goods are claimed (by another), the gift of the sack and house is complete, because the donor's hand was established over both the house and the goods in reality, so his delivery of them to the donee is valid. Then, upon the claim of the goods, if it becomes clear that the goods were not the donor's property, it does not become clear that the house was occupied by the donor's property — which is the preventer of complete possession. And every answer you have known regarding the gift of a house and sack along with what is in them is the answer regarding mortgage and charity, because possession is a condition for their completion as in the gift. End.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the rule of 'shaghil' and 'mashghul' in the context of gifts. The distinction is based on whether the gifted object is occupying the donor's property or is occupied by the donor's property. If a person gifts an object that is itself occupying the donor's property (e.g., food in a bag — the food occupies the bag), the gift is valid because the donor's property (the bag) is not preventing possession of the food. Conversely, if the gifted object is occupied by the donor's property (e.g., a bag containing food — the bag is occupied by the food which belongs to the donor), the gift is invalid because the donor's property is within the gifted object, thus preventing complete possession. The same principle applies to a saddled animal: gifting the animal with the saddle is invalid because the saddle (donor's property) occupies the animal; gifting only the saddle without the animal is valid. Then the text addresses a scenario where the gifted object is occupied by something not owned by the donor (e.g., a house with goods belonging to someone else). In that case, the gift is valid because the occupant is not the donor's property. The author provides various examples, including cases where the goods are later reclaimed, and concludes that the same rule applies to mortgage (rahn) and charity (sadaqa).

Key Terms
شاغل (shaghil): A gifted object that occupies or is placed on the donor's property, e.g., food in a bag owned by the donor.
مشغول (mashghul): A gifted object that is occupied by the donor's property, e.g., a bag containing the donor's food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person gifts a horse with its saddle. The saddle is the property of the donor. According to the text, what is the ruling?
A) The gift is valid because the horse is the main object.
B) The gift is invalid because the horse is occupied by the donor's saddle.
C) The gift is valid if the donee accepts it.
D) The gift is voidable and can be ratified.

Key Takeaway
A gift is valid only if the gifted object is not occupied by the donor's property; otherwise, it is void.

Possession of a Gifted House: Key, Division, and Permission
Ruling statement with expansions on possession modes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for valid possession of a gifted house, including key possession, division requirements for divisible property, and the effect of donor permission versus prohibition.

Core Idea
Possessing the key = possessing the house; for divisible property, division is needed for complete possession.

We continue with the rules of possession (qabd) in gifts. The passage clarifies that a house occupied by the donor's property prevents completion, but occupancy by a non-donor's property does not. It then details how possession is achieved: by key, by division for divisible property, and by subordination for indivisible property. Finally, it distinguishes between possession in the session (valid by istihsan without permission) and after the session (requires permission), and special cases when the object is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle of key possession
The text states that taking possession of the key of a house constitutes possession of the house itself. Recognize this as a specific Hanafi rule for immovables.
Key possession is sufficient even if you do not enter the house.
2
Differentiate between divisible and indivisible property
For property that can be divided (e.g., shares of land), complete possession requires taking possession of the specific gifted portion directly, not as part of the whole. For indivisible property (e.g., a small house), possession of the whole suffices.
This relates to how the entire gift becomes fully owned.
3
Analyze the permission scenarios
Map out three cases: (a) donor forbids possession – invalid always; (b) donor neither permits nor forbids – possession in session valid by istihsan, after session invalid; (c) absent object – possession requires donor’s permission.
Note the consistent distinction between qiyas (strict analogy) and istihsan (equity).
4
Understand the role of qiyas vs istihsan
The text repeatedly contrasts qiyas and istihsan. Qiyas would require explicit permission for any possession; istihsan relaxes this for possession in the gift session to facilitate the gift.
This is a key feature of Hanafi methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتصح إن قبض في مجلسها بلا إذن، أو بعده بإذن
[۱] فقبض مفتاح الدار قبض لها، والقبضُ الكامل فيما يحتمل القسمة بالقسمة حتى يقع القبض على الموهوب بطريق الأصالة من غير أن يكون القبضُ بتبعيَّةِ قبض الكل ، وفيما لا يحتمل القسمة بتبعية الكل.
[۲] فتصح إن قبضَ في مجلسها بلا إذن، أو بعده بإذن) : أي إذا قبض في المستعير كانت الهبة تامة، وإن تبين أن الدار مشغولة بما ليس بموهوب لما لم تكن مشغولة بملك الواهب، وهو المانع من تمام الهبة، ... الخ. وفي التفسير: ولو نهى عن القبض بعد الهبة لا يصح القبضُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده ، ولا يملكه قياساً، ولو لم يأذن له بالقبض، ولم ينه عنه إن قبضَ في المجلس صح القبضُ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن قبض بعد المجلس لا يصح القبضُ قياساً واستحساناً، ولو كان الموهوب غائباً فذهب وقبض، فإن كان القبض بإذن الواهب جازَ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن كان بغير إذنه لا يجوز. ينظر: «جامع الرموز» (٢ : ٦٠).
So it is valid if he takes possession in its session without permission, or after it with permission. [1] So possession of the key of the house is possession of it. And complete possession in what can be divided is by division, so that possession occurs over the gifted object in a primary manner, not by way of being subsidiary to possession of the whole. And in what cannot be divided, it is by being subsidiary to the whole. [2] 'So it is valid if he takes possession in its session without permission, or after it with permission' means: if he takes possession from the borrower, the gift is complete, even if it becomes clear that the house is occupied by what is not the gifted object, because it was not occupied by the donor's property, which is the preventer of the gift's completion. ... In the explanation: If he forbids possession after the gift, possession is not valid either in the session or after it, and he does not own by analogy. If he neither permits nor forbids, and he takes possession in the session, it is valid by istihsan, not by analogy. If he takes possession after the session, it is not valid by qiyas or istihsan. If the gifted object is absent and he goes and takes possession, if it is with the donor's permission, it is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas; if without his permission, it is not permissible. See: 'Jami' al-Rumuz' (2:60).
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage covers two main points: (1) Possession of a house that is occupied by non-donor's property is valid, as continued from the previous lesson. (2) Detailed rules regarding the mode of possession and permission. The text states that taking possession of the key constitutes possession of the house. For divisible property, complete possession is achieved by taking possession of the specific share directly, not as a subsidiary to the whole. For indivisible property, possession of the whole suffices. The second part discusses the effect of the donor's permission on possession. The default ruling is that possession in the session of the gift without explicit permission is valid by istihsan (equity), but not by qiyas (analogy). Possession after the session requires explicit permission; otherwise it is invalid. If the gifted object is not present, possession after going to it is valid only with the donor's permission by istihsan. These details are drawn from later Hanafi works like Jami' al-Rumuz.

Key Terms
قبض المفتاح (qabd al-miftah): Taking possession of the key of a house constitutes possession of the house itself for the purpose of completing the gift.
القسمة (al-qisma): Division of a divisible property (e.g., shares of land) to achieve independent possession of the gifted portion.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission from the donor for the donee to take possession; affects validity of possession after the gift session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A donor gives a house as a gift and says nothing. The donee takes the keys in the same meeting. Later, the donor says 'I forbid it.' Which is correct?
A) The gift is invalid because the donor forbade.
B) The gift is valid because possession in the session is valid by istihsan regardless of later forbiddance.
C) The gift is valid only if the donee returns the keys.
D) The gift is suspended until the donor permits.

Key Takeaway
Possession by key is sufficient for a house; for divisible property, specific division is required; permission rules differ between in-session and after-session possession.

Possession Without Permission in Gifts: The Hanafi Istihsan
Explaining when possession validates a gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qabd without explicit permission in the gift session and explain the istihsan argument that overrides the qiyas objection.

Core Idea
Possession without permission in the gift session is valid by istihsan—the gift itself implies authorization.

The validity of a gift (hibah) in Hanafi fiqh hinges on possession (qabd). But what if the donee takes possession without the donor's explicit say-so? This passage from a Hanafi commentary resolves the tension between strict analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan), declaring that the gift itself is an implied permission. We will unpack this reasoning and the practical rules that follow.

Guided Path
1
State the Core Ruling
Identify the central rule: the gift is valid if possession is taken in the session without permission, or after the session with permission.
The phrase 'فَتَصِحُّ إِنْ قَبَضَ فِي مَجْلِسِهَا بِلَا إِذْنٍ، أَوْ بَعْدَهُ بِإِذْنٍ' is the key.
2
Recognize the Qiyas Objection
Understand why, by strict analogy (qiyas), possession without permission would be invalid: the donor still owns the property, so any disposition requires his authorization.
Imam al-Shafi'i held this position.
3
Analyze the Istihsan Override
Examine the istihsan argument: possession is like acceptance (qabul) in a contract; the offer (ijab) itself implies authorization to accept.
وجه الاستحسان: إنَّ القبض كالقبول في الهبة من حيث إنّه يتوقف عليه ثبوت الملك، فيكون الإيجاب منه تسليطا على القبض.
4
Map the Detailed Scenarios
Follow the summary of rules: explicit permission, explicit forbiddance, silence, and absent property. Note how the ruling changes with the donor's expression.
The passage distinguishes between permission in the session, after the session, and for absent property.
5
Identify the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Understand the difference in daily practice: Hanafis consider the gift complete immediately upon possession in the session; Shafi'is require explicit permission, making such a gift invalid.
This directly affects the validity of many informal gifts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الهبة تعريفها وأحكامها فتصح إن قبض في مجلسها بلا إذن، أو بعده بإذن [۱] فقبض مفتاح الدار قبض لها، والقبضُ الكامل فيما يحتمل القسمة بالقسمة حتى يقع القبض على الموهوب بطريق الأصالة من غير أن يكون القبضُ بتبعيَّةِ قبض الكل ، وفيما لا يحتمل القسمة بتبعية الكل. فتصح إن قبضَ في مجلسها بلا إذن، أو بعده بإذن) (۲) : أي إذا قبض في المستعير كانت الهبة تامة، وإن تبين أن الدار مشغولة بما ليس بموهوب لما لم تكن مشغولة بملك الواهب، وهو المانع من تمام الهبة. وكذلك لو وهب داراً بما فيها من المتاع، أو وهـب جـوالـق بما فيه من المتاع ، وسلّمها إلى الموهوب ثم استحق المتاع، فالهبة تامة في الجوالق والدار ؛ لأنَّ يد الواهب كانت ثابتة على الدار، والمتاعُ جميعاً حقيقة فصح تسليمه إياها إلى الموهوب. ثم باستحقاق المتاعِ إن تبين أنَّ المتاعَ لم يكن ملك الواهب لم يتبين أن الدار كانت مشغولة بملك الواهب، وهو المانع من تمام القبض، وكل جواب عرفته في هبة الدار والجوالق بما فيها فهو الجواب في الرهن والصدقة ؛ لأنَّ القبض شرط تمامها كالهية. انتهى. [١] قوله : فقبض...الخ ؛ يعني فأخذ مفتاحَ الدَّارِ الموهوبة قبض لتلك الدار الموهوبة، بخلاف ما لو وهب ثياباً في صندوق مقفل، ورفع الصندوق لا يكون قبضاً فلا تتم الهبة. [٢]قوله : فتصح ... الخ ؛ هذا تفريع على أن القبض من تمام الهبة، فلو قبض (۱) يعني أن قبض بعض ما يقسم في ضمن الكل لا يفيد الملك حتى لو وهب نصف دار غير مقسوم ودفع الدار إليه فباع الموهوب له ما وهب له لا يجوز بيعه بمنزلة من باع هبة لم يقبضها. ينظر : «الشرنبلالية»(۲ : ۲۱۸). (۲) بيانها : أنه إذا أذنَ بالقبض صريحاً يصح قبضه في المجلس ،وبعده ، ويملكه قياساً واستحساناً، ولو نهى عن القبض بعد الهبة لا يصح القبضُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده ، ولا يملكه قياساً، ولو لم يأذن له بالقبض، ولم ينه عنه إن قبضَ في المجلس صح القبضُ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن قبض بعد المجلس لا يصح القبضُ قياساً واستحساناً، ولو كان الموهوب غائباً فذهب وقبض، فإن كان القبض بإذن الواهب جازَ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن كان بغير إذنه لا يجوز. ينظر: «جامع الرموز» (٢ : ٦٠). كمشاع لا يُقْسَمُ)) : متعلق بقوله فتصح ، والمراد به أنه إذا قسم لا يبقى منفعة ، كالرحى، والحمام، والبيت الصغير الموهوب الموهوب له في مجلس الهبة بلا إذن صريح من الواهب صح استحساناً، والقياس أنه لا يصح، وهو قول الشافعي له ؛ لأنَّ القبض تصرُّف في ملك الواهب إذ ملكه قبل القبض باق بدليل صحة تصرفه من البيع والاعتاق، فلا يصح بدون القبض بدون إذنه، وتمام الهبة موقوف على تمام القبض. ووجه الاستحسان : إنَّ القبض كالقبول في الهبة من حيث إنّه يتوقف عليه ثبوتُ وهو الملك، فيكون الإيجاب منه تسليطا على القبض، ولو قبضه بعد مجلس الهبة بإذن الواهب تصح أيضاً، لا بدون إذنه ؛ لأنا أثبتنا التسليط فيه إلحاقاً له بالقبول، والقبول يتقيّد بالمجلس؛ لأنَّ الدلالة لا تعمل بمقابلة التصريح ؛ فلهذا لو نهاه عن القبض لا يصح قبضُهُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده. حکمه، والحاصل : إنه إذا أذنَ بالقبض صريحاً يصح قبضه في المجلس وبعده ، ويملكه قياساً واستحساناً، ولو نهى عن القبض بعد الهبة لا يصح القبضُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده، ولا يملكه قياساً، ولو لم يأذن له بالقبض ، ولم ينه عنه إن قبض في المجلس صح القبض استحساناً لا قياساً ، وإن قبض بعد المجلس لا يصح القبض قياساً واستحساناً. ولو كان الموهوب غائباً فذهب وقبض، فإن كان القبض بإذن الواهب جازَ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن كان بغير إذنه لا يجوز، قال القُهُسْتانِي (٢) : لكنه مخالف لما ذكرنا من التأويلات. انتهى. ولا يخفى عليك إمكان التوفيق بأن وضع ماله في طريق ليكونَ ملكاً للرافع إذن بالقبض دلالة فيجوز فلا مخالفة أصلا(۳).
The book of gift: its definition and rulings. So it is valid if he takes possession in its session without permission, or after it with permission. [1] So taking the key of the house is possession for it, and complete possession in what can be divided is by division so that possession falls on the gifted thing in a primary way without being by way of following possession of the whole, and in what cannot be divided, it is by following the whole. And likewise, if he gave a house including its furniture, or gave a sack including its contents, and handed it over to the donee, then the furniture is reclaimed, the gift is valid regarding the sack and the house. Then by the reclamation of the furniture, if it becomes clear that the furniture was not the property of the donor, it does not become clear that the house was occupied by the property of the donor, which is the obstacle to complete possession. And every answer you know in the gift of the house and sack including what is in them is the answer in mortgage and charity. [1] His saying: 'So taking the key...' means taking the key of the gifted house is possession for that gifted house. [2] His saying: 'So it is valid...' is a branching on that possession is part of the completion of the gift. So if he takes possession in the session without explicit permission, it is valid by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not valid, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Because possession is a disposition in the property of the donor, since his ownership remains before possession, as evidenced by the validity of his disposition like sale and manumission. The face of istihsan: possession is like acceptance in gift in that the establishment of ownership depends on it, so the offer from him is an authorization for possession. And if he takes possession after the session with permission of the donor, it is also valid, not without his permission. The summary: if he explicitly permits possession, his possession is valid in the session and afterwards, and he owns it by qiyas and istihsan. If he forbids possession after the gift, possession is not valid in the session or afterwards. If he neither permits nor forbids, if he takes possession in the session, it is valid by istihsan not by qiyas; if after, it is not valid by either. If the gifted item is absent and he goes and takes possession, if with permission it is valid by istihsan not by qiyas; if without permission, not valid. Al-Qahistani said: but it contradicts the interpretations we mentioned. And it is not hidden from you the possibility of reconciliation by his placing his property in the road to be owned by the finder is implied permission, so it is valid, so no contradiction at all.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the conditions of qabd (possession) in a gift (hibah). The author begins by stating the core ruling: a gift is valid if possession is taken in the gift session without explicit permission, or after the session with explicit permission. The commentary explains that taking the key of a house constitutes possession of the house, analogous to taking possession of a locked chest. Complete possession for divisible property is achieved by taking a divided share, while for indivisible property it is by taking the whole. The discussion then addresses a scenario where a house is gifted along with its furniture, and the furniture is later reclaimed by a third party; the gift of the house remains valid because the donor's hand was established over both. The passage then delves into the juristic reasoning: the default rule by qiyas (analogy) is that possession without permission is invalid because the donor's ownership persists. However, istihsan (juristic preference) overrides this, treating the gift itself as an implied authorization for possession, similar to acceptance (qabul) in a contract. The Shafi'i school maintains the qiyas position, requiring explicit permission. The passage concludes by summarizing the detailed rules: when the donor explicitly permits, forbids, or remains silent, and in cases of absent property. It also reconciles a potential contradiction by noting that implied permission suffices.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the gifted item, which is necessary for the completion of the gift.
هبة (hibah): A gift; the transfer of ownership of a specific asset without compensation.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; deviating from qiyas in favor of a ruling based on a stronger evidence or necessity.
مشاع (mushā‘): An undivided share in property that is not partitioned; typically indivisible in practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is the gift valid if the donee takes possession of the gifted item in the gift session without the donor's explicit permission?
A) Yes, by istihsan because the gift itself implies permission.
B) No, explicit permission is always required.
C) Only if the property is divisible.
D) Only if the donor is present.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the gift itself implies permission for possession in the session, making the gift valid without explicit authorization.

Hibat al-Musha': Validity Conditions and the Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi ruling on hibat al-musha' with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting an undivided share (musha'), distinguish between divisible and indivisible property, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concepts of qabd and qiyas.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided share is only valid if the property cannot be divided without loss of utility.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah tackles a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the validity of gifting an undivided share (musha') in jointly owned property. The Hanafi school restricts such gifts to indivisible property, while the Shafi'i school permits them generally. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the role of possession (qabd) in completing a gift and how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the gift of an undivided share (hibat al-musha'). The Hanafi school rules that it is valid only in property that cannot be divided without losing utility (la yuqsam).
The key distinction is divisibility of the property.
2
Understand the role of possession (qabd)
In Hanafi law, a gift is not complete without possession (qabd) by the donee with the donor's permission. The passage discusses how possession can be implied (istihsan) or explicit, and its timing relative to the gift sitting.
The text differentiates scenarios of permission, silence, and prohibition.
3
Analyze the istihsan vs. qiyas reasoning
The Hanafi school uses istihsan (equitable preference) to allow possession without explicit permission in the same sitting, by analogy with acceptance (qabul). Qiyas (strict analogy) would require explicit permission. The disagreement with the Shafi'i is also framed as a clash of qiyas: Shafi'i analogizes gift to sale; Hanafi distinguishes because possession is a condition for completion, not for validity.
Qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) underlies the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the Shafi'i opposition and response
The Shafi'i school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) permits hibat al-musha' in all cases, citing the Quranic verse (2:237) and analogy with sale. The Hanafi response argues that the verse concerns mahr, not hibah, and that possession in a gift is a condition for completion, unlike sale.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is whether ownership transfers.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to a scenario
Given a real case: if someone gifts half of a divisible house, the gift is invalid (batil) in the Hanafi school. If the property is a small room that cannot be divided, the gift is valid (sahih) with deficient possession.
The text also notes that muhayah (alternating use) may be obligatory in indivisible property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كمشاع لا يُقْسَمُ زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية مجلس الهبة بلا إذن كان قبضاً ; لأنَّ الهبة دليل الإذن، وبعد إنقضاء مجلس الإذن لا بد أن يأذن الواهب صريحاً ، كمشاع لا يُقْسَمُ)) : متعلق بقوله فتصح ، والمراد به أنه إذا قسم لا يبقى منفعة ، كالرحى، والحمام، والبيت الصغير الموهوب الموهوب له في مجلس الهبة بلا إذن صريح من الواهب صح استحساناً، والقياس أنه لا يصح، وهو قول الشافعي له ; لأنَّ القبض تصرُّف في ملك الواهب إذ ملكه قبل القبض باق بدليل صحة تصرفه من البيع والاعتاق، فلا يصح بدون القبض بدون إذنه، وتمام الهبة موقوف على تمام القبض. ووجه الاستحسان : إنَّ القبض كالقبول في الهبة من حيث إنّه يتوقف عليه ثبوتُ وهو الملك، فيكون الإيجاب منه تسليطا على القبض، ولو قبضه بعد مجلس الهبة بإذن الواهب تصح أيضاً، لا بدون إذنه ; لأنا أثبتنا التسليط فيه إلحاقاً له بالقبول، والقبول يتقيّد بالمجلس; لأنَّ الدلالة لا تعمل بمقابلة التصريح ; فلهذا لو نهاه عن القبض لا يصح قبضُهُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده. حکمه، والحاصل : إنه إذا أذنَ بالقبض صريحاً يصح قبضه في المجلس وبعده ، ويملكه قياساً واستحساناً، ولو نهى عن القبض بعد الهبة لا يصح القبضُ لا في المجلس ولا بعده، ولا يملكه قياساً، ولو لم يأذن له بالقبض ، ولم ينه عنه إن قبض في المجلس صح القبض استحساناً لا قياساً ، وإن قبض بعد المجلس لا يصح القبض قياساً واستحساناً. ولو كان الموهوب غائباً فذهب وقبض، فإن كان القبض بإذن الواهب جازَ استحساناً لا قياساً، وإن كان بغير إذنه لا يجوز، قال القُهُسْتانِي : لكنه مخالف لما ذكرنا من التأويلات. انتهى. ولا يخفى عليك إمكان التوفيق بأن وضع ماله في طريق ليكونَ ملكاً للرافع إذن بالقبض دلالة فيجوز فلا مخالفة أصلا. لا فيما يُقْسَم) : أي لا تصح الهبة في مشاع لو قسم يبقى منفعته عندنا، خلافاً للشافعي وهذا الخلاف مبني على اشتراط القبض، هو يقول المشاع محل للقبض كما في البيع ونحوه ودابة واحدة ، أو لا يبقى منتفعاً بـه بعـد القسمة من جنس الانتفاع الذي كان قبل القسمة كالبيت الصغير والحمار الصغير، والثوب الصغير. كذا في «الدرر» وإنما صح فيه الهبة ; لأنَّ القبض لا يتصوّر فيه إلا بالقبض الناقص، وهو قبض الكل فاكتفى به، قال في «البحر» : هبة المشاع فيما لا ينقسم تفيد الملك للموهوب له على وجه لا يستحق المطالبة بالقسمة ; لأنها لا تمكن. وأما المهايأة فلا تجب في ظاهر الرواية ; لأنها إعارة ، فإنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ منهما يصير معيراً نصيبه من صاحبه، والجبر على الإعارة غير مشروع، وفي رواية: تجب. انتهى. والذي يفيده الزيلعي أنه يجبر على المهايأة ; لأنها قسمة المنافع والتبرع وقع في الغير فيكون إيجاباً في غير ما تبرع به، فلا يبالي به، وإنما المحظور الإيجاب في عين ما تبرع وقال قاضي زاده بعد نقل أنّ المهايأة لا تجب مع صلة عن صاحب «غاية البيان»: لعل هذا الجواب غير صحيح; لأنَّ التهايؤ يجب، ويجري فيه جبر القاضي إذا طلبه أحد الشركاء، ولا سيّما فيما لا يقسم ، نص عليه في عامة الكتب. كذا في «حاشية العلامة طحطاوي على الدر المختار قوله : خلافا للشافعي ; قال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد : تصح هبة المشاع سواء احتمل القسمة أو لا ; لقوله : فَيَصفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ إِلَّا أَن يَعْقُونَ أَوْ
[Beginning of passage: 'As an undivided share that cannot be divided...] The sitting of the gift without permission was possession, because the gift is evidence of permission. After the sitting of permission ends, the donor must explicitly permit. 'As an undivided share that cannot be divided' is attached to his saying 'so it is valid.' What is meant by it is that if it is divided, no benefit remains, like a handmill, a bathhouse, and a small house. The gift to the donee in the sitting of the gift without explicit permission from the donor is valid by istihsan, but by qiyas it is not valid, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because possession is a disposal in the ownership of the donor since his ownership remains before possession, as evidenced by the validity of his disposal through sale and manumission. So it is not valid without possession without his permission, and the completion of the gift is suspended on the completion of possession. The aspect of istihsan: that possession is like acceptance in the gift in that the establishment of ownership depends on it, so the offer from him is authorization for possession. If he takes possession after the sitting of the gift with the permission of the donor, it is also valid, not without his permission, because we have established authorization in it by analogy with acceptance, and acceptance is restricted to the sitting, because indication does not work in the face of explicit statement. For this reason, if he forbids possession, his possession is not valid, neither in the sitting nor after. Its ruling and summary: If he explicitly permits possession, his possession is valid in the sitting and after, and he owns it by qiyas and istihsan. If he forbids possession after the gift, possession is not valid neither in the sitting nor after, and he does not own it by qiyas. If he does not permit possession nor forbid it, if he takes possession in the sitting, it is valid by istihsan, not by qiyas. If he takes possession after the sitting, it is not valid by qiyas and istihsan. If the gifted object is absent and he goes and takes possession, if the possession is with the donor's permission, it is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas. If without his permission, it is not permissible. Al-Quhistani said: 'But it contradicts the interpretations we mentioned.' End. It is not hidden from you the possibility of reconciliation by his placing his property in the road to become ownership of the rafi'? Permission for possession by indication, so it is permissible, so there is no contradiction at all. [He said:] 'Not in what is divided': That is, the gift in an undivided share that if divided its benefit remains is not valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. This disagreement is based on the requirement of possession. He says the undivided share is a locus for possession as in sale and the like. 'One slave or one animal, or what is not benefited from after division in the same type of benefit that existed before division, like a small house, a small donkey, a small garment.' As in al-Durar. [The gift in it is valid] only because possession cannot be conceived in it except with deficient possession, which is possession of the entire thing, so it sufficed. He said in al-Bahr: The gift of an undivided share in what does not divide gives ownership to the donee in a way that he does not deserve to demand division, because it is not possible. As for alternating use (muhayah), it is not obligatory in the apparent narration because it is a loan, since each of them becomes a lender of his share to his companion, and compulsion for lending is not legislated. In one narration it is obligatory. End. What al-Zayla'i indicates is that he is compelled to alternate use, because it is a division of benefits, and the donation occurred in something else, so it becomes an obligation in something other than what he donated, so it is not taken into account. The only prohibition is obligation in the very thing donated. Qadi Zada said after transmitting that alternating use is not obligatory with a connection from the author of Ghayat al-Bayan: 'Perhaps this answer is not correct, because alternating use is obligatory, and the judge's compulsion applies if one of the partners requests it, especially in what cannot be divided, as stated in most books.' As in Hashiyat al-Allama al-Tahtawi ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. 'He said: Contrary to al-Shafi'i; al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: The gift of an undivided share is valid whether it can be divided or not, because of His saying: "فَيَصفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ إِلَّا أَن يَعْقُونَ أَوْ"' [Surah al-Baqarah 2:237, incomplete].
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage from the book of hibah (gift) in the commentary on al-Wiqayah presents the Hanafi ruling on the gift of an undivided share (musha'). The author begins by explaining the condition of possession (qabd) in the gift. The Hanafi school holds that possession by the donee in the same sitting of the gift is valid by istihsan (equitable reasoning) even without explicit permission, because the offer itself implies authorization. By analogy (qiyas), possession without permission would be invalid. The text details three scenarios: explicit permission, explicit prohibition, and silence. The ruling that the gift of an undivided share is valid only if the property cannot be divided without loss of utility (like a small house or a mill) is then given. This is a point of disagreement with the Shafi'i school, which allows the gift of musha' in all cases, arguing that an undivided share is capable of possession just like in a sale. The Hanafi response relies on the fact that possession in an indivisible property is only possible as a deficient possession (qabd naqis) of the whole, which suffices. The passage then discusses the obligation of alternating use (muhayah) for such properties, noting a difference of opinion: in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) it is not obligatory, but some later authorities (like al-Zayla'i and Qadi Zada) hold it is obligatory and compellable by the judge. The passage concludes by citing the Shafi'i proof from the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:237). The mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school is that the gift of musha' in indivisible property is valid, and muhayah is obligatory if requested by a partner.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha'): An undivided share in a jointly owned property (shuyu').
قبض (qabd): Physical taking possession by the donee, a condition for completion of the gift in Hanafi law.
هبة (hibah): A contract of gift transferring ownership without compensation.
مهايأة (muhayah): Alternating use of an undivided property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on gifting an undivided share (musha') in a property that can be divided without losing utility?
A) The gift is valid because the gift contract is complete upon offer and acceptance.
B) The gift is valid only if the donee takes possession with explicit permission.
C) The gift is invalid because possession of an undivided share is not possible in divisible property.
D) The gift is valid if the property is small.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a gift of an undivided share is valid only if the property cannot be divided without losing utility; otherwise, it is invalid due to the impossibility of proper possession.

Ruling on Gifting Undivided Shares: The Hanafi-Shafiʿi Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on mushāʿ gift and muhāyāʾ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting mushāʿ, distinguish between divisible and indivisible property, and evaluate the Shafiʿi counterarguments.

Core Idea
Gift of a divisible mushaʿ is invalid because perfect possession is impossible.

Gifting an undivided share in property (mushāʿ) is a common transaction, but the Hanafi school imposes a critical condition: valid possession (qabd) must be complete. This leads to a sharp disagreement with the Shafiʿis, who allow such gifts in all cases. This lesson unpacks the rationale, proofs, and practical consequences of this dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Determine the ruling on gifting mushāʿ: valid or invalid, and under what conditions (divisible vs indivisible property).
2
Analyse the opposing Shafiʿi view
Understand the Shafiʿi position (along with Malik and Ahmad) that all gifts of mushaʿ are valid, and list their three main proofs: Quran 2:237, Hadith of Hawazin, and analogy to sale.
3
Examine the Hanafi refutations
For each Shafiʿi proof, see how the Hanafi school responds: the verse refers to debt, the hadith occurred after division, and sale is not a gratuitous contract.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Given a property like a large house (divisible) or a small donkey (indivisible), state whether the gift is valid and explain why.
5
Optional: Explore the subsidiary ruling on muhāyāʾ
Understand the Hanafi debate on alternating use (muhāyāʾ): the apparent narration says it is not obligatory, but later authorities (al-Zaylaʿī, Qāḍī Zādah) hold that a judge can compel it for indivisible property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الهبة / تعريفها وأحكامها
لا فيما يُقْسَم
لا فيما يُقسم) : أي لا تصح الهبة في مشاع لو قسم يبقى منفعته عندنا، خلافاً للشافعي
وهذا الخلاف مبني على اشتراط القبض، هو يقول المشاع محل للقبض كما في البيع ونحوه ودابة واحدة ، أو لا يبقى منتفعاً بـه بعـد القسمة من جنس الانتفاع الذي كان قبل القسمة كالبيت الصغير والحمار الصغير، والثوب الصغير. كذا في «الدرر»
وإنما صح فيه الهبة ؛ لأنَّ القبض لا يتصوّر فيه إلا بالقبض الناقص، وهو قبض الكل فاكتفى به، قال في «البحر» : هبة المشاع فيما لا ينقسم تفيد الملك للموهوب له على وجه لا يستحق المطالبة بالقسمة ؛ لأنها لا تمكن.
وأما المهايأة فلا تجب في ظاهر الرواية ؛ لأنها إعارة ، فإنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ منهما يصير معيراً نصيبه من صاحبه، والجبر على الإعارة غير مشروع، وفي رواية: تجب. انتهى. والذي يفيده الزيلعي) أنه يجبر على المهايأة ؛ لأنها قسمة المنافع والتبرع وقع في الغير فيكون إيجاباً في غير ما تبرع به، فلا يبالي به، وإنما المحظور الإيجاب في عين ما تبرع
وقال قاضي زاده بعد نقل أنّ المهايأة لا تجب مع صلة عن صاحب «غاية البيان»: لعل هذا الجواب غير صحيح؛ لأنَّ التهايؤ يجب، ويجري فيه جبر القاضي إذا طلبه أحد الشركاء، ولا سيّما فيما لا يقسم ، نص عليه في عامة الكتب. كذا في «حاشية العلامة طحطاوي على الدر المختار )
قوله : خلافا للشافعي ؛ قال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد : تصح هبة المشاع سواء احتمل القسمة أو لا ؛ لقوله : فَيَصفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ إِلَّا أَن يَعْقُونَ أَوْ يَعْقُوا الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ، عُقدَةُ النكاح ) ، فإنّه يقتضي أن الصداق إذا كان عيناً يتنصفُ بالطلاق قبل الدخول، ويندبُ كلُّ واحدٍ من الزوجين إلى ترك الكل للآخر، وذلك هبةُ المشاع.
ولِما في «صحيح البخاري» من أن وفد هوازن لَمَّا جاؤوا يطلبون من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يرد عليهم ما عنده منهم ، قال : ما كان لي ولبني عبد المطلب فهو لكم»، وهذه هبة مشاع ؛ ولأنه عقد تمليك ، فيصح في المشاع كالبيع بأنواعه.
ولنا : إنَّ في تجويز عقدِ الهبة في المشاع المنقسم إلزام الواهب شيئاً لم يلتزمه ، وهو القسمة، فيكون عقد التبرع موجباً لضمان القسمة، وهو خلاف موضوع التبرع ، بخلاف ما لا يحتمل القسمة ؛ لأنَّ القبض لا يتصور فيه إلا ناقصاً فاكتفى به.
والجواب عن الآية : إنَّ العفو حقيقة في الدِّينِ دون العين، وإسقاط الدِّينِ جائز مشاعاً كان أو غير مشاع ؛ لأنه غير محتاج إلى القبض، وفي العين كل واحد منهما مندوب إلى العفو عندنا ، ولكن بأن يهب نصيبه لصاحبه بعد القسمة، وليس في الآية ما يمنع ذلك. وعن الحديث : إن ذلك كان بعد القسمة، وعن القياس : إنَّ البيع يتم بلا قبض، وأيضاً إنه ليس عقد تبرع حتى يلزم خلاف موضوع التبرع.
قوله : ونحن نقول ... الخ ؛ تقريره : إنَّ القبض منصوص عليه في الهبة، فيشترط وجوده على وجه الكمال، كما أنَّ استقبال القبلة لما كان منصوصاً عليه يشترط وجوده على وجه الكمال، حتى لو استقبل الحجرَ لا تجوز صلاته مع أنّ كونه من البيت ثابت بالسنة.
على أنَّ القبض ثبت مطلقاً، والمطلق يتناول الكامل، والكامل هو الموجود من كل وجه، والقبض في المشاع موجود من وجه دون وجه ؛ لأنَّ القبض عبارة عن كون الشيء في حيز القابض، والمشاعُ ليس في حيّزه من كلّ وجه؛ لأنه في حيزه من وجه،
Book of Gift / Its Definition and Rulings
Not in what can be divided
'Not in what can be divided': meaning the gift of a mushaʿ (undivided share) is not valid if after division its benefit remains, according to us, contrary to al-Shafiʿi.
This disagreement is based on the condition of possession (qabd). He (al-Shafiʿi) says that a mushaʿ is a place for possession as in sale and the like, and a single riding animal, or that after division one does not remain benefiting from it in the same kind of benefit as before division, like a small house, a small donkey, and a small garment. Thus in 'al-Durar'.
And it is valid in it because qabd is only conceivable with deficient qabd, which is taking possession of the whole, so it suffices. He said in 'al-Bahr': The gift of a mushaʿ in what is indivisible confers ownership on the donee in a manner that he does not have the right to demand division because it is not possible.
As for alternating use (muhāyāʾ), it is not obligatory in the apparent narration because it is a loan; each of them becomes a lender of his share to the other, and compulsion for lending is not legislated. In one narration: it is obligatory. End. What al-Zaylaʿī indicates is that he is compelled to alternate because it is a division of benefits, and the donation occurred in something else, thus it is an obligation in something other than what was donated, so it is not paid attention to; the prohibition is only in obligating the very thing donated.
Qadi Zādah said after quoting that muhāyāʾ is not obligatory from the author of 'Ghāyat al-Bayān': Perhaps this answer is incorrect because alternating use is obligatory and the judge compels it if one of the partners requests it, especially what is indivisible; this is stated in most books. Thus in 'Hāshiyat al-ʿAllāmah al-Ṭaḥṭāwī ʿalā al-Durr al-Mukhtār'.
His statement: 'contrary to al-Shafiʿi'; al-Shafiʿi, Malik, and Ahmad said: The gift of a mushaʿ is valid whether it is likely to be divided or not, because of His statement: 'So half of what you have fixed unless they forgive or he forgives in whose hand is the marriage tie' (Quran 2:237). For it implies that if the dower is a specific item, it is halved by divorce before consummation, and each spouse is urged to leave the whole to the other, and that is a gift of mushaʿ.
And because of what is in Sahih al-Bukhari, that when the delegation of Hawazin came asking the Prophet ﷺ to return what he had taken from them, he said: 'What belongs to me and the Banu Abd al-Muttalib is yours' — and this is a gift of mushaʿ. And because it is a contract of ownership, so it is valid in mushaʿ like all types of sale.
And our evidence: Allowing the gift contract in a divisible mushaʿ necessitates imposing something on the donor that he did not undertake, which is division. So a gratuitous contract would entail guaranteeing division, which is contrary to the nature of gratuity. Unlike what does not admit division, because qabd is only conceivable deficiently, so it is sufficed with it.
The answer regarding the verse: 'Forgiveness (ʿafw)' is in reality for debt, not for a specific item. Remitting a debt is valid whether it is a mushaʿ or not because it does not require qabd. For a specific item, each is urged to forgive according to us, but by gifting his share to the other after division, and there is nothing in the verse preventing that.
Regarding the hadith: That was after division.
Regarding the analogy: Sale is completed without qabd, and also it is not a gratuitous contract such that it would contradict the nature of gratuity.
His statement: 'And we say...' etc.; its explanation: Qabd is prescribed in gift, so its existence in a perfect manner is required, just as facing the qibla is prescribed, so its existence in perfection is required, to the extent that if one faces the Black Stone, his prayer is not valid even though its being from the Kaaba is established by Sunnah.
Moreover, qabd is established absolutely, and the absolute includes the perfect, and the perfect is what exists from every aspect. Qabd in mushaʿ exists from one aspect but not from another, because qabd means that the thing is in the possession of the take-holder; and mushaʿ is not in his possession from every aspect because it is in his possession from one aspect,
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of gifting an undivided share (mushāʿ) in property. The Hanafi school holds that a gift of a mushaʿ is invalid if the property is divisible, meaning that after hypothetical division each part can still be beneficially used in a manner similar to the whole (e.g., a large house or animal). The reason is that valid possession (qabd) is a condition for the gift contract, and in a divisible mushaʿ, the donee cannot achieve full and exclusive possession without actual division. However, if the property is indivisible (e.g., a small house or animal that would lose its utility if divided), the gift is valid because possession is only possible deficiently, and the law accepts it as sufficient. The passage then discusses the ruling on alternating use (muhāyāʾ) between co-owners: in the apparent narration it is not compulsory, but some later scholars hold that the judge can compel it, especially for indivisible property.
The Shafiʿi school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) disagrees and considers gifts of mushaʿ valid regardless of divisibility. Their proofs include the Quranic verse on the dower (2:237) which encourages forgiveness between spouses — understood as gifting one's share before division — and the hadith of the Hawazin delegation where the Prophet ﷺ gifted his share of captives without prior division. They also argue by analogy to sale, which is valid over a mushaʿ.
The Hanafi response refutes these: the verse refers to forgiveness of a debt, not a specific item, and if it is a specific item, the recommended act is to give after division. The hadith is interpreted as having occurred after division. The analogy to sale fails because sale is a commutative contract that does not require qabd for validity, whereas gift is gratuitous and requires perfected qabd. The final footnote elaborates that qabd is required in its complete form, analogizing to facing the qibla in prayer—partial facing is insufficient. Thus, in a divisible mushaʿ, qabd is incomplete because the property remains shared, so the gift is invalid.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gratuitous transfer of ownership in property during one's lifetime, requiring offer, acceptance, and possession.
مشاع (mushāʿ): An undivided share in a jointly owned property.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the gifted property by the donee.
مهايأة (muhāyāʾ): An agreement between co-owners to alternate the use of an undivided property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a gift of a divisible mushaʿ (undivided share) invalid?
A) Because the donor cannot unilaterally withdraw from the gift.
B) Because perfect possession (qabd) cannot be achieved without division.
C) Because the Quran prohibits giving undivided shares.
D) Because the gift contract requires witnessed offer and acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a gift of an undivided share is valid only if the property is indivisible; otherwise, the gift is invalid due to the impossibility of perfect possession.

Hiba al-Musha': The Hanafi Ruling on Gifting Undivided Shares
Defending the Hanafi position with analysis of Quran, hadith, and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting an undivided share in divisible property, identify the condition of complete possession that makes it invalid, and explain why the Hanafis rebut the opposing proofs from the Quran, hadith, and analogy to sale.

Core Idea
A gift requires complete possession; an undivided share cannot be fully possessed without partition, so the gift is invalid.

The permissibility of gifting an undivided share (hiba al-musha') has been a point of debate among jurists. The Hanafi school holds that such a gift is invalid if the property can be divided, because the condition of complete possession (qabd) cannot be satisfied. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi argument, how they address the opposing evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and legal analogy, and why Ibn Abi Layla's dissenting view is not taken as the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
In the passage, the author states the Hanafi position: a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid (fasid). The key condition is that possession (qabd) must be complete. Determine what 'complete possession' means and why an undivided share fails it.
Note that possession of a share is partial because the partner also has a claim.
2
Analyze the rebuttal of the Quranic verse (2:237)
Opponents cite Surah Al-Baqarah 2:237 encouraging spouses to pardon the dower. The Hanafis argue that 'afw (pardon) refers to remission of debt, not gifting a specific asset. Also, they say the encouragement is to gift after partition, not before. Identify the linguistic and contextual basis of this rebuttal.
3
Analyze the rebuttal of the hadith of Hawazin
The hadith where the Prophet ﷺ said to the delegation, 'What is mine and the Banu Abd al-Muttalib is yours,' is cited as evidence for gifting undivided shares. The Hanafis respond that this occurred after partition. Check what the passage says about this.
4
Examine the analogy (qiyas) to sale and its refutation
Opponents argue that since sale is valid without immediate possession, gift should also be valid. The Hanafis distinguish by noting that sale is a commutative contract, not gratuitous. Imposing an obligation to partition in a gratuitous contract contradicts its nature. Understand this distinction.
The passage also mentions that sale does require delivery (taslim), but the need for possession is different.
5
Distinguish concurrent vs. subsequent undividedness
The passage clarifies that undividedness arising after the gift (tari') does not invalidate it, but concurrent undividedness (muqarin), such as a claim (istihqaq) that proves the donor never owned the whole, does. Identify why this distinction matters.
This shows that the defect is at the time of the contract, not later.

ونحن نقول : القبضُ منصوص عليه هاهنا فلا بد من كماله. يَعْقُوا الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ، عُقدَةُ النكاح ) ، فإنّه يقتضي أن الصداق إذا كان عيناً يتنصفُ بالطلاق قبل الدخول، ويندبُ كلُّ واحدٍ من الزوجين إلى ترك الكل للآخر، وذلك هبةُ المشاع. ولِما في «صحيح البخاري» من أن وفد هوازن لَمَّا جاؤوا يطلبون من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يرد عليهم ما عنده منهم ، قال : ما كان لي ولبني عبد المطلب فهو لكم»، وهذه هبة مشاع ؛ ولأنه عقد تمليك ، فيصح في المشاع كالبيع بأنواعه. ولنا : إنَّ في تجويز عقدِ الهبة في المشاع المنقسم إلزام الواهب شيئاً لم يلتزمه ، وهو القسمة، فيكون عقد التبرع موجباً لضمان القسمة، وهو خلاف موضوع التبرع ، بخلاف ما لا يحتمل القسمة ؛ لأنَّ القبض لا يتصور فيه إلا ناقصاً فاكتفى به. والجواب عن الآية : إنَّ العفو حقيقة في الدِّينِ دون العين، وإسقاط الدِّينِ جائز مشاعاً كان أو غير مشاع ؛ لأنه غير محتاج إلى القبض، وفي العين كل واحد منهما مندوب إلى العفو عندنا ، ولكن بأن يهب نصيبه لصاحبه بعد القسمة، وليس في الآية ما يمنع ذلك. وعن الحديث : إن ذلك كان بعد القسمة، وعن القياس : إنَّ البيع يتم بلا قبض، وأيضاً إنه ليس عقد تبرع حتى يلزم خلاف موضوع التبرع. [1 قوله : ونحن نقول ... الخ ؛ تقريره : إنَّ القبض منصوص عليه في الهبة، فيشترط وجوده على وجه الكمال، كما أنَّ استقبال القبلة لما كان منصوصاً عليه يشترط وجوده على وجه الكمال، حتى لو استقبل الحجرَ لا تجوز صلاته مع أنّ كونه من البيت ثابت بالسنة. على أنَّ القبض ثبت مطلقاً، والمطلق يتناول الكامل، والكامل هو الموجود من كل وجه، والقبض في المشاع موجود من وجه دون وجه ؛ لأنَّ القبض عبارة عن كون الشيء في حيز القابض، والمشاعُ ليس في حيّزه من كلّ وجه؛ لأنه في حيزه من وجه، وفي حيّز شريكه من وجه، وتمامه لا يحصلُ إلا بالقسمة ؛ لأن تميز الأنصباء لا يحصل إلا بالقسمة، وهذا مما لا يقسم. [1]قوله : ولا فرق عندنا... الخ ؛ قال في «الفصول العمادية»: أما هبة المشاع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة تجوز من الشريكِ ومن الأجنبي، وفيما يحتملها فلا تجوز من الشريك ولا من الأجنبي. وقال قاضي خان الله في «فتاواه» : وهب نصيبه مما يقسم كالدارِ والأرض والمكيل والموزون من غير شريكه، لا يجوز عند الكلّ، وإن وهب من شريكه لا يجوز عندنا ، وقال ابن أبي ليلى له يجوز. انتهى. [٢] قوله : أو استحق... الخ ؛ فيه إنّه مخالف لما في «الكافي» و«الفصول العمادية»: إن الشيوع الطارئ لا يفسد الهبة بالاتفاق، وهو أن يرجع في بعض الهبة شائعاً ، أما الاستحقاق فيفسد الكلّ ؛ لأنه مقارن، كذا ذكر شيخ الإسلام أبو بكر له في (هبة) «المحيط». انتهى. ولذا قال في «الدر المختار (۳) : والمانع من تمام القبض شيوع مقارن للعقد لا طارئ ، كأن يرجع في بعضهما شائعاً ، فإنه لا يفسدها اتفاقاً، والاستحقاق شيوع مقارن لا طارئ فيفسد الكل، حتى لو وهب أرضاً وزرعاً وسلّمهما فاستحق الزرعُ بطلت في الأرض لاستحقاق البعض الشائع فيما يحتمل القسمة والاستحقاق إذا ظهر بالبينة فيكون مقارناً لها لا طارئاً كما زعمه صدر الشريعة له ، وإن تبعه ابن الكمال (۳) فتنبه. انتهى.
And we say: Possession is explicitly mentioned here, so it must be complete. The verse 'except that they pardon or the one in whose hand is the marriage knot' (Qur'an 2:237) implies that if the dower is a specific asset, it halves by divorce before consummation, and each spouse is encouraged to forego the whole in favor of the other, and that is a gift of an undivided share. And due to what is in Sahih al-Bukhari, that when the delegation of Hawazin came asking the Prophet ﷺ to return what he had of theirs, he said: 'What is mine and the Banu Abd al-Muttalib is yours,' and this is a gift of an undivided share. And because it is a contract of ownership, it is valid in undivided shares like sale in all its types. But we argue: Permitting a gift contract in an undivided share that is divisible imposes upon the donor something he did not undertake, namely partition, so a gratuitous contract would require guarantee of partition, which contradicts the nature of gratuitous contracts, unlike what cannot be divided, because possession in that case can only be incomplete, so it is sufficient. The answer regarding the verse: 'Afw (pardon) is literally used for debt, not for a specific asset; remission of debt is permissible whether it is undivided or not, because it does not require possession. As for a specific asset, each spouse is encouraged to pardon according to us, but by gifting one's share to the other after partition, and there is nothing in the verse preventing that. Regarding the hadith: That was after partition. Regarding the analogy: Sale is completed without possession, and also it is not a gratuitous contract so the objection of contradicting the nature of gratuitous contracts does not arise. [1] His statement: 'And we say... etc.' Its explanation: Possession is explicitly mentioned in gift, so its existence in a complete manner is required, just as facing the qibla, since it is mentioned, requires its existence in a complete manner, so that if one faces the Black Stone, his prayer is not valid, even though its being part of the Ka'bah is established by sunnah. Furthermore, possession is established in absolute terms, and the absolute includes the complete; the complete is what exists from every aspect. Possession of an undivided share exists from one aspect but not from another, because possession means the thing being in the domain of the possessor, and an undivided share is not in his domain from every aspect, as it is in his domain from one aspect and in his partner's domain from another, and its completion can only be achieved by partition, because the distinction of shares cannot be achieved except by partition, and this is something that cannot be divided. [1] His statement: 'There is no difference for us... etc.' He said in al-Fusul al-Imadiyya: As for the gift of an undivided share in something that cannot be divided, it is valid from a partner and from a stranger; but in something that can be divided, it is not valid from a partner nor from a stranger. Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: If one gifts his share in something divisible, like a house, land, or measured or weighed items, to someone other than his partner, it is not valid according to all; if he gifts it to his partner, it is not valid according to us, but Ibn Abi Layla said it is valid. End. [2] His statement: 'Or if a claim arises... etc.' In it, it is contrary to what is in al-Kafi and al-Fusul al-Imadiyya: That subsequent undividedness (tari') does not invalidate the gift by consensus, such as when one returns part of the gift as undivided; while a claim (istihqaq) invalidates the whole because it is concurrent (muqarin). This is what Shaykh al-Islam Abu Bakr mentioned in (Gift) of al-Muhit. End. Hence it is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The preventer of complete possession is undividedness concurrent with the contract, not subsequent, such as if one returns part of it as undivided, it does not invalidate by consensus. And a claim is concurrent, not subsequent, so it invalidates the whole; even if one gifts land and crops and hands both over, then the crops are claimed, the gift of the land becomes invalid because part of an undivided share in something divisible was claimed. And if the claim appears through evidence, it is concurrent with it, not subsequent, as Sadr al-Shari'ah claimed, even if Ibn al-Kamal followed him. So be alert. End.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling and proof regarding the permissibility of gifting an undivided share (hiba al-musha') in property that can be divided. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: possession (qabd) is required for a gift, and it must be complete. He then addresses the opposing view which uses the Quranic verse 2:237 (encouraging pardon of dower) and a hadith about the delegation of Hawazin as evidence that gifting undivided shares is valid. The Hanafi response clarifies that 'afw in the verse refers to remitting a debt, not transferring a specific asset; it does not require possession. The hadith is interpreted as occurring after partition. Regarding the analogy (qiyas) with sale, the Hanafis argue that sale is not a gratuitous contract, so the objection about imposing an obligation of partition does not apply. The author then explains that possession in an undivided share is incomplete because the property is partly in the domain of the partner; complete possession requires partition. The commentary further distinguishes between undividedness that arises after the contract (tari')—which does not invalidate the gift—and undividedness that is concurrent (muqarin), such as a claim that proves the property was never fully owned, which invalidates the gift. The passage also notes the disagreement of Ibn Abi Layla, who allowed gifting undivided shares to a partner, but the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that it is not allowed, regardless of whether the recipient is a partner or a stranger. The key legal principle is that a gratuitous contract cannot impose obligations not voluntarily undertaken, such as the cost and effort of partition.

Key Terms
هبة المشاع (hibat al-musha'): A gift of an undivided share in property that can be divided (e.g., half a house or land).
قبض (qabd): Physical or legal possession of the gifted item; a condition for the validity of a gift in Hanafi fiqh.
شيوع مقارن (shuyu' muqarin): Undividedness that exists at the time of the contract, as opposed to arising later (tari').
استحقاق (istihqaq): A claim by a third party that part of the gifted property rightfully belongs to them, proving the donor never had full ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school invalidate a gift of an undivided share in divisible property?
A) Because the Quran forbids any form of undivided ownership.
B) Because complete possession is impossible until the property is partitioned.
C) Because the Prophet ﷺ specifically prohibited such gifts.
D) Because the donor must always retain a share for themselves.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid because it fails the condition of complete possession; the donor must first partition the property.

Gifting an Undivided Share: Concomitant vs Supervening Shuyu'
States the rule that gifting a shuyu' is invalid and discusses istihqaq as concomitant shuyu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting an undivided share (shuyu') and distinguish between concomitant and supervening undividedness, including the istihqaq case.

Core Idea
Concomitant shuyu' invalidates the gift; supervening does not. Istihqaq is concomitant because it proves pre-existing undividedness.

In Hanafi law, gifting an undivided share of a divisible property raises a key distinction: does the undividedness exist at the contract (concomitant) or arise later (supervening)? This lesson unpacks the rule, its application to partners and strangers, and the special case where a third party claims (istihqaq) part of the gifted property, which is treated as concomitant undividedness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is gifting an undivided share (shuyu') of property that is divisible (e.g., land, house). The Hanafi ruling: such a gift is fasid (corrupt) unless the share is separated and delivered before or at the time of taking possession.
If the property is indivisible (e.g., a small well), the gift is valid.
2
Distinguish between concomitant and supervening shuyu'
Concomitant shuyu' (al-shuyu' al-muqarin) exists at the time of the contract and invalidates the gift. Supervening shuyu' (al-shuyu' al-tari') arises after the contract (e.g., donor takes back part) and does not invalidate by agreement.
The text emphasizes that the invalidating factor is concomitant, not supervening.
3
Apply to the istihqaq case
If a third party establishes a claim (istihqaq) to part of the gifted property through evidence, it is considered concomitant shuyu', because the right existed at the time of the contract. This invalidates the entire gift, unlike the view of Sadr al-Shari'ah who considered it supervening.
The claim is proven by evidence, so it retroactively shows undividedness at contract.
4
Determine the relevant time for shuyu'
The text clarifies that consideration is at the time of taking possession (qabd), not the contract. If the donor delivers a divided share after the contract, the gift is valid. Examples: gifting half a house and later delivering both halves; or gifting dates on a tree and handing them over after separation.
This allows curing an initial concomitant shuyu' by subsequent physical division before possession.

كتاب الهبة / تعريفها وأحكامها

ولا فرق عندنا بين أن يُهَب من الشريك أو من الأجنبي، والمفسد هو الشيوع المقارن، لا الشيوع الطارئ، كما إذا وهب، ثم رجع في البعض الشائع أو استحق البعض الشائع. وفي حيز شريكه من وجه، وتمامه لا يحصل إلا بالقسمة؛ لأن تميز الأنصباء لا يحصل إلا بالقسمة، وهذا مما لا يقسم.

[قوله: ولا فرق عندنا... الخ؛ قال في «الفصول العمادية»: أما هبة المشاع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة تجوز من الشريك ومن الأجنبي، وفيما يحتملها فلا تجوز من الشريك ولا من الأجنبي. وقال قاضي خان في «فتاواه»: وهب نصيبه مما يقسم كالدار والأرض والمكيل والموزون من غير شريكه، لا يجوز عند الكل، وإن وهب من شريكه لا يجوز عندنا، وقال ابن أبي ليلى: له يجوز. انتهى.

قوله: أو استحق... الخ؛ فيه إنه مخالف لما في «الكافي» و«الفصول العمادية»: إن الشيوع الطارئ لا يفسد الهبة بالاتفاق، وهو أن يرجع في بعض الهبة شائعاً، أما الاستحقاق فيفسد الكل؛ لأنه مقارن، كذا ذكر شيخ الإسلام أبو بكر في (هبة) «المحيط». انتهى. ولذا قال في «الدر المختار»: والمانع من تمام القبض شيوع مقارن للعقد لا طارئ، كأن يرجع في بعضهما شائعاً، فإنه لا يفسدها اتفاقاً، والاستحقاق شيوع مقارن لا طارئ فيفسد الكل، حتى لو وهب أرضاً وزرعاً وسلّمهما فاستحق الزرع بطلت في الأرض لاستحقاق البعض الشائع فيما يحتمل القسمة والاستحقاق إذا ظهر بالبينة فيكون مقارناً لها لا طارئاً كما زعمه صدر الشريعة، وإن تبعه ابن الكمال فتنبه. انتهى.

(والعبرة في الشيوع وقت القبض لا وقت العقد، حتى لو وهب مشاعاً وسلّم مقسوماً يجوز، وكذا لو وهب نصف الدار ولم يُسَلّم ثم وهب النصف الآخر وسلّمه جازت الهبة، أو وهب تمراً في نخل أو زرعاً في أرض ثم سَلّم بعد ذلك مفرزاً يجوز. ينظر: «البناية» ٧: ٨٠٨).
The Book of Gift / Its Definition and Rulings

There is no distinction in our school between whether the gift is from a partner or a stranger; the invalidating factor is concomitant undividedness, not supervening undividedness, as when he gave and then took back part of the undivided share or part of the undivided share was established by claim. And it is in the sphere of his partner in a way, and its completion is only achieved by division, because the separation of shares is only achieved by division, and this is something that cannot be divided.

[His saying: There is no distinction in our school, etc.; said in al-Fusul al-Imadiyyah: As for the gift of undivided property that cannot be divided, it is permissible from a partner and from a stranger; and what can be divided, it is not permissible from a partner nor from a stranger. And Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: He gifted his share of what is divisible, such as a house and land and measured and weighed items, from other than his partner, it is not permissible by all; and if he gifted from his partner, it is not permissible in our school, and Ibn Abi Layla said it is permissible. End.

His saying: Or established by claim, etc.; in it, it contradicts what is in al-Kafi and al-Fusul al-Imadiyyah: Supervening undividedness does not invalidate the gift by agreement, and it is that he takes back part of the gift as undivided; as for establishment by claim, it invalidates the whole because it is concomitant. Thus mentioned Shaykh al-Islam Abu Bakr in (Gift) of al-Muhit. End. And for this it is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The preventive of complete taking possession is concomitant undividedness at the time of contract, not supervening, such as taking back part of it as undivided; it does not invalidate it by agreement; and establishment by claim is concomitant undividedness, not supervening, so it invalidates the whole. Even if he gave land and crops and handed them over, and the crops were established by claim, it invalidates the land because of the establishment of undivided part of what is divisible; and establishment by claim, if it appears by evidence, is concomitant to it, not supervening, as Sadr al-Shari'ah claimed, and Ibn al-Kamal followed him, so beware. End.

(And the consideration regarding undividedness is at the time of taking possession, not at the time of contract, so that if he gave an undivided share and delivered it divided, it is permissible; similarly, if he gave half the house and did not hand over, then gave the other half and handed over the whole, the gift is permissible; or if he gave dates on a palm tree or crops on land, then handed over after separation, it is permissible. See al-Binayah 7:808).
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the general principle for gifts of undivided shares (shuyu') in Hanafi law. The author clarifies that the key invalidating factor is not whether the donee is a partner or a stranger, but rather whether the undividedness is concomitant (muqarin) at the time of contract or supervening (tari'). Concomitant undividedness invalidates the gift if the property is divisible, while supervening does not. The text then addresses a specific case: if the donee establishes a claim (istihqaq) to part of the gifted property after the gift, that is considered concomitant undividedness because the right existed at the time of contract, even if proven later. This invalidates the entire gift. The author refutes the view of Sadr al-Shari'ah, who considered it supervening. The footnote at the end emphasizes that the relevant time for considering undividedness is at the time of taking possession (qabd), not the contract, giving examples where division before delivery makes the gift valid.

Key Terms
الشيوع المقارن (al-shuyu' al-muqarin): Undividedness that exists at the time of the contract (e.g., gifting a half share without separation).
الشيوع الطارئ (al-shuyu' al-tari'): Undividedness that arises after the contract (e.g., the donor takes back part of the gift).
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): A third party's claim to part of the gifted property that is proven by evidence, considered concomitant shuyu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi law, if someone gifts an undivided share of a divisible house and later a third party successfully claims (istihqaq) part of the house, what is the effect on the gift?
A) The gift remains valid, and the claim affects only the claimed portion.
B) The gift is invalidated entirely because istihqaq is considered concomitant undividedness.
C) The gift is suspended until the claim is resolved.
D) The gift is valid if the donee is a partner.

Key Takeaway
Gifting an undivided share in divisible property is invalid due to concomitant shuyu'; istihqaq is treated as concomitant, thus invalidating the entire gift.

Validity of Gift of Undivided Share and Gift of Non-Existent Item
Explains that gift of undivided share becomes valid if divided and delivered, and discusses gifts of undifferentiated mixtures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a gift of an undivided share to become valid, and explain why gifts of potential items (like flour in wheat) are invalid.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided share is fasid but curable; a gift of a non-existent item is batil forever.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘āyah clarifies two essential rules in Hanafi gift law. First, gifting an undivided share (shā‘i‘) is initially corrupt (fasid) but becomes valid if the donor later divides and delivers a specific portion. Second, gifting an item that does not yet actually exist—such as flour mixed in wheat or oil in sesame—is invalid from the start, even if the donor later processes and delivers it. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for determining the enforceability of a gift contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) a gift of an undivided share (e.g., half a house) followed by division and delivery, and (2) a gift of a potential item (e.g., flour in wheat) that is not yet extracted.
These are separate rulings with different rationales.
2
Determine the condition that cures the first scenario
For the undivided share, the gift becomes valid only after actual division (qismah) and delivery (taslim) of a specific share. The commentary stresses that completion (tamām) depends on possession (qabd), and at the time of possession there must be no undividedness.
Compare: The contract itself is initially valid, but the gift is not complete until delivery removes the shuyū‘.
3
Determine the reason for invalidity in the second scenario
For mixed items like flour in wheat, the gifted object does not actually exist at the time of the contract—it is only potential. Existence in potential (bi’l-quwwa) is not legally recognized, so the gift is void (bāṭil) from the outset.
Even subsequent grinding and delivery do not cure the initial non-existence.
4
Note the temporal focus: condition at delivery vs. contract
In the first scenario, the critical time for removing undividedness is delivery, not the contract. In the second scenario, the critical time for existence is the contract—if the item is non-existent then, the gift is void regardless of later events.
This distinction explains why the undivided share gift can be cured, but the mixed item gift cannot.
5
Apply the principles to new cases
Use these rules to evaluate hypothetical gifts: e.g., gifting milk in an unmilked goat (non-existent) vs. gifting half a cow (undivided, curable).
Always check whether the item existed at contract time and whether undividedness is resolved at delivery.

Source Text
